It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\\n36:  *\\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \\\"use strict\\\" code. The \\\"use strict\\\" bit is stored in\\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\\n48:  *\\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\\n50:  * different groups of flags:\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"are we parsing strict code?\\\", and so\\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\\n57:  * \\\"returned up\\\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"did we see a use strict\\n58:  * directive\\\"?\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\\n63:  *\\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\\n90:  *\\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\\n93:  *\\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\\n96:  *\\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\\n103:  */\\n104: \\n105: class JSFunction;\\n106: class JSObject;\\n107: class JSScript;\\n108: struct /* -*- Mode: C++; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sts=2 et sw=2 tw=80:\n3:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\n4:  * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this\n5:  * file, You can obtain one at http://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */\n6: \n7: #ifndef frontend_BytecodeCompiler_h\n8: #define frontend_BytecodeCompiler_h\n9: \n10: #include \"mozilla/AlreadyAddRefed.h\"  // already_AddRefed\n11: #include \"mozilla/Maybe.h\"            // mozilla::Maybe\n12: #include \"mozilla/Utf8.h\"             // mozilla::Utf8Unit\n13: \n14: #include <stdint.h>  // uint32_t\n15: \n16: #include \"ds/LifoAlloc.h\"                 // js::LifoAlloc\n17: #include \"frontend/FunctionSyntaxKind.h\"  // FunctionSyntaxKind\n18: #include \"frontend/ScriptIndex.h\"         // ScriptIndex\n19: #include \"js/CompileOptions.h\"  // JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions, JS::PrefableCompileOptions\n20: #include \"js/GCVector.h\"    // JS::StackGCVector\n21: #include \"js/Id.h\"          // JS::PropertyKey\n22: #include \"js/RootingAPI.h\"  // JS::Handle\n23: #include \"js/SourceText.h\"  // JS::SourceText\n24: #include \"js/UniquePtr.h\"   // js::UniquePtr\n25: #include \"js/Value.h\"       // JS::Value\n26: #include \"vm/ScopeKind.h\"   // js::ScopeKind\n27: \n28: /*\n29:  * Structure of all of the support classes.\n30:  *\n31:  * Parser: described in Parser.h.\n32:  *\n33:  * BytecodeCompiler.cpp: BytecodeCompiler.h\n34:  * This is the \"driver\", the high-level operations like \"compile this source to\n35:  * bytecode\". It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\n36:  *\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\n41:  *\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \"use strict\" code. The \"use strict\" bit is stored in\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\n48:  *\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\n50:  * different groups of flags:\n51:  *\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \"passed down\"\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"are we parsing strict code?\", and so\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\n55:  *\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\n57:  * \"returned up\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"did we see a use strict\n58:  * directive\"?\n59:  *\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\n63:  *\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n67:  * can be optimized away.\n68:  *\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\n80:  *\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\n82:  *\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \"pass-down\"\n84:  * data and some \"return-up\" data.\n85:  *\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\n90:  *\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\n93:  *\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\n96:  *\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\n99:  *\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\n103:  */\n104: \n105: class JSFunction;\n106: class JSObject;\n107: class JSScript;\n108: struct This tree is\\n248:  * not a concrete syntax tree in all respects (for example, || and && are left\\n249:  * associative, but (A && B && C) translates into the right-associated tree\\n250:  * <A && <B && C>> so that code generation can emit a left-associative branch\\n251:  * around <B && C> when A is false). Limit,\\n262:   Start = LastUnused + 1,\\n263:   BinOpFirst = ParseNodeKind::CoalesceExpr,\\n264:   BinOpLast = ParseNodeKind::PowExpr,\\n265:   AssignmentStart = ParseNodeKind::AssignExpr,\\n266: Certain limitations of\\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\\n28:  *\\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\\n30:  *\\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\\n35:  *\\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\\n37:  *\\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\\n49:  *\\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\\n54:  * to \\\"create an arguments object for a function\\\" obviously varies between\\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\\n58:  *\\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\\n61:  * further below).\\n62:  *\\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\\n67:  *\\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\\n78:  *     character type.\\n79:  *\\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\\n81:  * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n84:  * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\\n85:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive.  As\\n86:  * noted above, this field's existence separate from that in ParserBase\\n87:  * motivates the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameters on various token stream\\n88:  * classes.\\n89:  *\\n90:  * Everything in PerHandlerParser *could* be folded into GeneralParser (below)\\n91:  * if desired.  We don't fold in this manner because all such functions would\\n92:  * be instantiated once per Unit -- but if exactly equivalent code would be\\n93:  * generated (because PerHandlerParser functions have no awareness of Unit),\\n94:  * it's risky to *depend* upon the compiler coalescing the instantiations into\\n95:  * one in the final binary.  PerHandlerParser guarantees no duplication.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * == Parser<ParseHandler, Unit> final → GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> ==\\n98:  *\\n99:  * The final (pun intended) axis of complexity lies in Parser.\\n100:  *\\n101:  * Some functionality depends on character type, yet also is defined in\\n102:  * significantly different form in full and syntax parsing.  For example,\\n103:  * attempting to parse the source text of a module will do so in full parsing\\n104:  * but immediately fail in syntax parsing -- so the former is a mess'o'code\\n105:  * while the latter is effectively |return null();|.  Such functionality is\\n106:  * defined in Parser<SyntaxParseHandler or FullParseHandler, Unit> as\\n107:  * appropriate.\\n108:  *\\n109:  * There's a crucial distinction between GeneralParser and Parser, that\\n110:  * explains why both must exist (despite taking exactly the same template\\n111:  * parameters, and despite GeneralParser and Parser existing in a one-to-one\\n112:  * relationship).  GeneralParser is one unspecialized template class:\\n113:  *\\n114:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit>\\n115:  *   class GeneralParser : ...\\n116:  *   {\\n117:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n118:  *   };\\n119:  *\\n120:  * but Parser is one undefined template class with two separate\\n121:  * specializations:\\n122:  *\\n123:  *   // Declare, but do not define.\\n124:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit> class Parser;\\n125:  *\\n126:  *   // Define a syntax-parsing specialization.\\n127:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n128:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\\n129:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\\n130:  *   {\\n131:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n132:  *   };\\n133:  *\\n134:  *   // Define a full-parsing specialization.\\n135:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n136:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\\n137:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\\n138:  *   {\\n139:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n140:  *   };\\n141:  *\\n142:  * This odd distinction is necessary because C++ unfortunately doesn't allow\\n143:  * partial function specialization:\\n144:  *\\n145:  *   // BAD: You can only specialize a template function if you specify *every*\\n146:  *   //      template parameter, i.e. ParseHandler *and* Unit.\\n147:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n148:  *   void\\n149:  *   GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>::foo() {}\\n150:  *\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-150\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0f32b745-310b-4e57-9e68-6b38379087ea","uuid":"38e60bc2-10d8-4ab6-a278-f1c0cdc96427","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C++; GeneralParser is one unspecialized template class:\\n113:  *\\n114:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit>\\n115:  *   class GeneralParser : ...\\n116:  *   {\\n117:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n118:  *   };\\n119:  *\\n120:  * but Parser is one undefined template class with two separate\\n121:  * specializations:\\n122:  *\\n123:  *   // Declare, but do not define.\\n124:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit> class Parser;\\n125:  *\\n126:  *   // Define a syntax-parsing specialization.\\n127:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n128:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\\n129:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\\n130:  *   {\\n131:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n132:  *   };\\n133:  *\\n134:  *   // Define a full-parsing specialization.\\n135:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n136:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\\n137:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\\n138:  *   {\\n139:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n140:  *   };\\n141:  *\\n142:  * This odd distinction is necessary because C++ unfortunately doesn't allow\\n143:  * partial function specialization:\\n144:  *\\n145:  *   // BAD: You can only specialize a template function if you specify *every*\\n146:  *   //      template parameter, i.e. ParseHandler *and* Unit.\\n147:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n148:  *   void\\n149:  *   GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>::foo() {}\\n150:  *\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-150\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /* -*- Mode: C++; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sts=2 et sw=2 tw=80:\n3:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\n4:  * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this\n5:  * file, You can obtain one at http://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */\n6: \n7: /* JS parser. */\n8: \n9: #ifndef frontend_Parser_h\n10: #define frontend_Parser_h\n11: \n12: /*\n13:  * [SMDOC] JS Parser\n14:  *\n15:  * JS parsers capable of generating ASTs from source text.\n16:  *\n17:  * A parser embeds token stream information, then gets and matches tokens to\n18:  * generate a syntax tree that, if desired, BytecodeEmitter will use to compile\n19:  * bytecode.\n20:  *\n21:  * Like token streams (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h), parser\n22:  * classes are heavily templatized -- along the token stream's character-type\n23:  * axis, and also along a full-parse/syntax-parse axis.  Certain limitations of\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\n28:  *\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\n30:  *\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\n35:  *\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\n37:  *\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n41:  *\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\n49:  *\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\n51:  *\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\n54:  * to \"create an arguments object for a function\" obviously varies between\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\n58:  *\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\n61:  * further below).\n62:  *\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\n64:  *\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\n67:  *\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\n78:  *     character type.\n79:  *\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\n81:  * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\n82:  *\n83:  * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n84:  * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\n85:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive.  As\n86:  * noted above, this field's existence separate from that in ParserBase\n87:  * motivates the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameters on various token stream\n88:  * classes.\n89:  *\n90:  * Everything in PerHandlerParser *could* be folded into GeneralParser (below)\n91:  * if desired.  We don't fold in this manner because all such functions would\n92:  * be instantiated once per Unit -- but if exactly equivalent code would be\n93:  * generated (because PerHandlerParser functions have no awareness of Unit),\n94:  * it's risky to *depend* upon the compiler coalescing the instantiations into\n95:  * one in the final binary.  PerHandlerParser guarantees no duplication.\n96:  *\n97:  * == Parser<ParseHandler, Unit> final → GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> ==\n98:  *\n99:  * The final (pun intended) axis of complexity lies in Parser.\n100:  *\n101:  * Some functionality depends on character type, yet also is defined in\n102:  * significantly different form in full and syntax parsing.  For example,\n103:  * attempting to parse the source text of a module will do so in full parsing\n104:  * but immediately fail in syntax parsing -- so the former is a mess'o'code\n105:  * while the latter is effectively |return null();|.  Such functionality is\n106:  * defined in Parser<SyntaxParseHandler or FullParseHandler, Unit> as\n107:  * appropriate.\n108:  *\n109:  * There's a crucial distinction between GeneralParser and Parser, that\n110:  * explains why both must exist (despite taking exactly the same template\n111:  * parameters, and despite GeneralParser and Parser existing in a one-to-one\n112:  * relationship).  GeneralParser is one unspecialized template class:\n113:  *\n114:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit>\n115:  *   class GeneralParser : ...\n116:  *   {\n117:  *     ...parsing functions...\n118:  *   };\n119:  *\n120:  * but Parser is one undefined template class with two separate\n121:  * specializations:\n122:  *\n123:  *   // Declare, but do not define.\n124:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit> class Parser;\n125:  *\n126:  *   // Define a syntax-parsing specialization.\n127:  *   template<typename Unit>\n128:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\n129:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\n130:  *   {\n131:  *     ...parsing functions...\n132:  *   };\n133:  *\n134:  *   // Define a full-parsing specialization.\n135:  *   template<typename Unit>\n136:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\n137:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\n138:  *   {\n139:  *     ...parsing functions...\n140:  *   };\n141:  *\n142:  * This odd distinction is necessary because C++ unfortunately doesn't allow\n143:  * partial function specialization:\n144:  *\n145:  *   // BAD: You can only specialize a template function if you specify *every*\n146:  *   //      template parameter, i.e. ParseHandler *and* Unit.\n147:  *   template<typename Unit>\n148:  *   void\n149:  *   GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>::foo() {}\n150:  *\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-150"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CMN2jodRGZLcNCeM32N8EX","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sw=2 et tw=0 ft=c:\\n3:  *\\n4:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\\n5:  * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this\\n6:  * file, You can obtain one at http://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */\\n7: \\n8: #ifndef vm_Opcodes_h\\n9: #define vm_Opcodes_h\\n10: \\n11: #include <stddef.h>\\n12: #include <stdint.h>\\n13: \\n14: #include \\\"js/TypeDecls.h\\\"\\n15: \\n16: // clang-format off\\n17: /*\\n18:  * [SMDOC] Bytecode Definitions\\n19:  *\\n20:  * SpiderMonkey bytecode instructions.\\n21:  *\\n22:  * To use this header, define a macro of the form:\\n23:  *\\n24:  *     #define MACRO(op, op_snake, token, length, nuses, ndefs, format) ...\\n25:  *\\n26:  * Then `FOR_EACH_OPCODE(MACRO)` invokes `MACRO` for every opcode.\\n27:  *\\n28:  * Field        Description\\n29:  * -----        -----------\\n30:  * op           UpperCamelCase form of opcode id\\n31:  * op_snake     snake_case form of opcode id\\n32:  * token        Pretty-printer string, or null if ugly\\n33:  * length       Number of bytes including any immediate operands\\n34:  * nuses        Number of stack slots consumed by bytecode, -1 if variadic\\n35:  * ndefs        Number of stack slots produced by bytecode\\n36:  * format       JOF_ flags describing instruction operand layout, etc.\\n37:  *\\n38:  * For more about `format`, see the comments on the `JOF_` constants defined in\\n39:  * BytecodeUtil.h.\\n40:  *\\n41:  *\\n42:  * [SMDOC] Bytecode Invariants\\n43:  *\\n44:  * Creating scripts that do not follow the rules can lead to undefined\\n45:  * behavior. Bytecode has many consumers, not just the interpreter: JITs,\\n46:  * analyses, the debugger. That's why the rules below apply even to code that\\n47:  * can't be reached in ordinary execution (such as code after an infinite loop\\n48:  * or inside an `if (false)` block).\\n49:  *\\n50:  * The `code()` of a script must be a packed (not aligned) sequence of valid\\n51:  * instructions from start to end. Each instruction has a single byte opcode\\n52:  * followed by a number of operand bytes based on the opcode.\\n53:  *\\n54:  * ## Jump instructions\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Operands named `offset`, `forwardOffset`, or `defaultOffset` are jump\\n57:  * offsets, the distance in bytes from the start of the current instruction to\\n58:  * the start of another instruction in the same script. Operands named\\n59:  * `forwardOffset` or `defaultOffset` must be positive.\\n60:  *\\n61:  * Forward jumps must jump to a `JSOp::JumpTarget` instruction.  Backward jumps,\\n62:  * indicated by negative offsets, must jump to a `JSOp::LoopHead` instruction.\\n63:  * Jump offsets can't be zero.\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Needless to say, scripts must not contain overlapping instruction sequences\\n66:  * (in the sense of <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overlapping_gene>).\\n67:  *\\n68:  * A script's `trynotes` and `scopeNotes` impose further constraints. Each try\\n69:  * note and each scope note marks a region of the bytecode where some invariant\\n70:  * holds, or some cleanup behavior is needed--that there's a for-in iterator in\\n71:  * a particular stack slot, for instance, which must be closed on error. All\\n72:  * paths into the span must establish that invariant. In practice, this means\\n73:  * other code never jumps into the span: the only way in is to execute the\\n74:  * bytecode instruction that sets up the invariant (in our example,\\n75:  * `JSOp::Iter`).\\n76:  *\\n77:  * If a script's `trynotes` (see \\\"Try Notes\\\" in JSScript.h) contain a\\n78:  * `JSTRY_CATCH` or `JSTRY_FINALLY` span, there must be a `JSOp::Try`\\n79:  * instruction immediately before the span and a `JSOp::JumpTarget immediately\\n80:  * after it. Instructions must not jump to this `JSOp::JumpTarget`. (The VM puts\\n81:  * us there on exception.) Furthermore, the instruction sequence immediately\\n82:  * following a `JSTRY_CATCH` span must read `JumpTarget; Exception` or, in\\n83:  * non-function scripts, `JumpTarget; Undefined; SetRval; Exception`. (These\\n84:  * instructions run with an exception pending; other instructions aren't\\n85:  * designed to handle that.)\\n86:  *\\n87:  * Unreachable instructions are allowed, but they have to follow all the rules.\\n88:  *\\n89:  * Control must not reach the end of a script. (Currently, the last instruction\\n90:  * is always JSOp::RetRval.)\\n91:  *\\n92:  * ## Other operands\\n93:  *\\n94:  * Operands named `nameIndex` or `atomIndex` (which appear on instructions that\\n95:  * have `JOF_ATOM` in the `format` field) must be valid indexes into\\n96:  * `script->atoms()`.\\n97:  *\\n98:  * Operands named `argc` (`JOF_ARGC`) are argument counts for call\\n99:  * instructions. `argc` must be small enough that the instruction's nuses is <=\\n100:  * the current stack depth (see \\\"Stack depth\\\" below).\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/vm/Opcodes.h%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0f32b745-310b-4e57-9e68-6b38379087ea","uuid":"cc5e166e-9b87-4e85-a383-d600f8ea208a","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sw=2 et tw=0 ft=c:\\n3:  *\\n4:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\\n5:  * License, v. 2.0. Bytecode has many consumers, not just the interpreter: JITs,\\n46:  * analyses, the debugger. That's why the rules below apply even to code that\\n47:  * can't be reached in ordinary execution (such as code after an infinite loop\\n48:  * or inside an `if (false)` block).\\n49:  *\\n50:  * The `code()` of a script must be a packed (not aligned) sequence of valid\\n51:  * instructions from start to end. Backward jumps,\\n62:  * indicated by negative offsets, must jump to a `JSOp::LoopHead` instruction.\\n63:  * Jump offsets can't be zero.\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Needless to say, scripts must not contain overlapping instruction sequences\\n66:  * (in the sense of <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overlapping_gene>).\\n67:  *\\n68:  * A script's `trynotes` and `scopeNotes` impose further constraints. Compilation Entry Point (BytecodeCompiler)\\n\\n**File**: `js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h` and `js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.cpp`\\n\\nThe main entry point is `CompileGlobalScript()` (declared in BytecodeCompiler.h at lines 145-153), which serves as the high-level driver for compilation. This function orchestrates the entire compilation process:\\n\\n- Takes source text and compile options as input\\n- Creates a `ScriptCompiler<Unit>` object to manage the compilation state\\n- Initializes the compilation environment with the parser and allocators\\n- Calls the compiler's `compile()` method to parse and emit bytecode\\n- Instantiates the resulting stencil into a `JSScript` object\\n\\nAdditional entry points include:\\n- `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilWithInput()` - compiles to an intermediate stencil format\\n- `CompileEvalScript()` - specifically for eval code compilation (line 180-184)\\n- `InstantiateStencils()` - converts stencil data structures to executable JSScript objects (line 134-141)\\n\\n## 2. Tokenization (TokenStream)\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h` and `js/src/frontend/TokenStream.cpp`\\n\\nBefore parsing, the source text is tokenized by `TokenStream` class. The tokenizer breaks the source text into individual tokens (identifiers, keywords, operators, literals, etc.), which the parser then consumes.\\n\\n## 3. Parser and AST Generation\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/frontend/Parser.h` and `js/src/frontend/Parser.cpp`\\n\\nThe parser is implemented through a template hierarchy:\\n- `ParserSharedBase` - base class with shared functionality\\n- `ParserBase` - base for all JS parsers, manages token stream and error handling\\n- `PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler>` - parses with handler-specific logic (full vs. syntax parsing)\\n- `GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit>` - template implementation handling both character types and parse modes\\n- `Parser<ParseHandler, Unit>` - final specialization for full parsing (FullParseHandler) or syntax-only parsing (SyntaxParseHandler)\\n\\nThe parser's main entry point is the `parse()` method (inherited through the hierarchy), which:\\n- Reads tokens from the TokenStream\\n- Builds an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) of ParseNode objects\\n- Validates syntax according to ECMAScript specifications\\n- Collects scope and binding information\\n\\n## 4. AST Node Types (ParseNode)\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.cpp`\\n\\nThe AST is composed of `ParseNode` objects representing different JavaScript constructs. Key node types include:\\n\\n- **Literals**: `NumericLiteral`, `BigIntLiteral`, `StringExpr`, `RegExpLiteral`, `BooleanLiteral`, `NullLiteral`\\n- **Expressions**: `BinaryNode` (binary operators), `UnaryNode` (unary operators), `ConditionalExpression` (ternary operator), `AssignmentNode`\\n- **Function-related**: `FunctionNode` (function declarations/expressions), `CallNode` (function calls), `NewExpr`\\n- **Statements**: `StatementList`, `IfStmt` (TernaryNode), `WhileStmt`, `DoWhileStmt`, `ForStmt`, `SwitchStatement`, `TryStmt`\\n- **Declarations**: `DeclarationListNode` (var/let/const), `ClassNode`\\n- **Access**: `PropertyAccess` (dot notation), `PropertyByValue` (bracket notation), `CallNode` (function calls)\\n- **Control Flow**: `BreakStatement`, `ContinueStatement`, `LabeledStatement`, `ReturnStmt`\\n\\nAll node types are defined through the `FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND` macro (lines 63-244 in ParseNode.h), which enumerates approximately 180+ distinct parse node kinds.\\n\\n## 5. Bytecode Emitter\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h` and `js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.cpp`\\n\\nThe `BytecodeEmitter` class (declared in BytecodeEmitter.h starting at line 77) converts the AST to bytecode instructions. Key responsibilities include:\\n\\n- **AST Traversal**: Walks the ParseNode tree generated by the parser\\n- **Opcode Emission**: Generates bytecode instructions (JSOp operations) for each AST node\\n- **Scope Management**: Uses `EmitterScope` to track variable bindings and determine which opcodes are needed\\n- **Jump Resolution**: Handles forward/backward jumps for control flow (if/else, loops, switches)\\n- **Bytecode Sections**: Separates bytecode into prologue (variable/function setup) and main sections\\n- **Data Generation**: Collects GC things (atoms, constants, inner functions) into `PerScriptData` structures\\n\\nThe emitter works with helper classes for specific constructs:\\n- `FunctionEmitter` - for function definitions\\n- `IfEmitter` - for if statements\\n- `WhileEmitter`, `DoWhileEmitter`, `ForOfEmitter` - for loops\\n- `TryEmitter` - for try/catch/finally\\n- `SwitchEmitter` - for switch statements\\n\\n## 6. Bytecode Instructions (Opcodes)\\n\\n**File**: `js/src/vm/Opcodes.h`\\n\\nThe bytecode instruction set is defined by the `JSOp` enum, which includes approximately 200+ operations such as:\\n\\n- **Stack Operations**: Push, Pop, Dup\\n- **Literals**: Int8, Int32, Double, String, Null, Undefined\\n- **Binary Operations**: Add, Sub, Mul, Div, Mod, Pow, BitAnd, BitOr, etc.\\n- **Comparison**: Eq, Ne, Lt, Gt, Le, Ge, StrictEq, StrictNe\\n- **Variable Access**: GetLocal, SetLocal, GetArg, GetGName, SetGName\\n- **Property Access**: GetProp, SetProp, GetElem, SetElem, HasOwn\\n- **Function Calls**: Call, New, SpreadCall\\n- **Control Flow**: JumpIfTrue, JumpIfFalse, Jump, JumpTarget, LoopHead\\n- **Try/Catch**: Try, Catch, Throw\\n- **Return**: Return, RetRval\\n- **Special**: Nop, Debugger, Undefined, Null, True, False\\n\\nEach opcode has metadata defining its immediate operands, stack effects, and format flags.\\n\\n## 7. Bytecode Output (JSScript)\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/vm/JSScript.h` and `js/src/vm/JSScript.cpp`\\n\\nThe `JSScript` class (declared in JSScript.h) represents a compiled JavaScript script and contains:\\n\\n- **Bytecode**: The instruction stream produced by BytecodeEmitter (stored as packed bytes)\\n- **Constants/Atoms**: Identifiers and literal values used in the script\\n- **Try Notes**: Exception handling information (catch/finally ranges)\\n- **Scope Notes**: Lexical scope boundaries\\n- **Source Location Info**: Mapping between bytecode offsets and source line/column numbers\\n- **Function Objects**: Pointers to compiled inner functions\\n- **Flags**: Metadata about script type (global, function, eval, module) and properties\\n- **Script Data**: Shared immutable data (ImmutableScriptData) storing code, atoms, and scope information\\n\\n## Compilation Pipeline Summary\\n\\nThe complete compilation chain for a global script is:\\n\\n```\\nSource Text (char16_t or Utf8Unit)\\n        ↓\\n   TokenStream::getToken()\\n        ↓ (tokenization)\\nTokens (SCRIPT_TOKEN, NAME_TOKEN, etc.)\\n        ↓\\n   Parser::parse()\\n        ↓ (parsing)\\nParseNode Tree (AST)\\n        ↓\\n   BytecodeEmitter::emit()\\n        ↓ (code generation)\\nBytecode Instructions (JSOp sequences)\\n        ↓\\n   CompilationStencil (intermediate format)\\n        ↓\\n   InstantiateStencils()\\n        ↓\\n   JSScript (executable bytecode)\\n        ↓\\n   Interpreter::run() or JIT Compilation\\n```\\n\\nKey architectural patterns:\\n- **Template-based polymorphism** for character types (char16_t vs Utf8Unit) and parse modes (full vs. syntax)\\n- **Two-phase compilation**: First create intermediate stencil data, then instantiate to GC objects\\n- **Lazy compilation**: Functions can be compiled on-demand rather than eagerly\\n- **Scope tracking**: Binding information flows through parsing and bytecode emission phases\\n- **Error recovery**: Errors are reported with source locations and context information\\n\\nThis design allows SpiderMonkey to efficiently compile JavaScript across different character encodings, support both immediate and deferred compilation, and enable various optimizations at each Bytecode Instructions (Opcodes)\\n\\n**File**: `js/src/vm/Opcodes.h`\\n\\nThe bytecode instruction set is defined by the `JSOp` enum, which includes approximately 200+ operations such as:\\n\\n- **Stack Operations**: Push, Pop, Dup\\n- **Literals**: Int8, Int32, Double, String, Null, Undefined\\n- **Binary Operations**: Add, Sub, Mul, Div, Mod, Pow, BitAnd, BitOr, etc.\\n- **Comparison**: Eq, Ne, Lt, Gt, Le, Ge, StrictEq, StrictNe\\n- **Variable Access**: GetLocal, SetLocal, GetArg, GetGName, SetGName\\n- **Property Access**: GetProp, SetProp, GetElem, SetElem, HasOwn\\n- **Function Calls**: Call, New, SpreadCall\\n- **Control Flow**: JumpIfTrue, JumpIfFalse, Jump, JumpTarget, LoopHead\\n- **Try/Catch**: Try, Catch, Throw\\n- **Return**: Return, RetRval\\n- **Special**: Nop, Debugger, Undefined, Null, True, False\\n\\nEach opcode has metadata defining its immediate operands, stack effects, and format flags.\\n\\n## 7. Bytecode Output (JSScript)\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/vm/JSScript.h` and `js/src/vm/JSScript.cpp`\\n\\nThe `JSScript` class (declared in JSScript.h) represents a compiled JavaScript script and contains:\\n\\n- **Bytecode**: The instruction stream produced by BytecodeEmitter (stored as packed bytes)\\n- **Constants/Atoms**: Identifiers and literal values used in the script\\n- **Try Notes**: Exception handling information (catch/finally ranges)\\n- **Scope Notes**: Lexical scope boundaries\\n- **Source Location Info**: Mapping between bytecode offsets and source line/column numbers\\n- **Function Objects**: Pointers to compiled inner functions\\n- **Flags**: Metadata about script type (global, function, eval, module) and properties\\n- **Script Data**: Shared immutable data (ImmutableScriptData) storing code, atoms, and scope information\\n\\n## Compilation Pipeline Summary\\n\\nThe complete compilation chain for a global script is:\\n\\n```\\nSource Text (char16_t or Utf8Unit)\\n        ↓\\n   TokenStream::getToken()\\n        ↓ (tokenization)\\nTokens (SCRIPT_TOKEN, NAME_TOKEN, etc.)\\n        ↓\\n   Parser::parse()\\n        ↓ (parsing)\\nParseNode Tree (AST)\\n        ↓\\n   BytecodeEmitter::emit()\\n        ↓ (code generation)\\nBytecode Instructions (JSOp sequences)\\n        ↓\\n   CompilationStencil (intermediate format)\\n        ↓\\n   InstantiateStencils()\\n        ↓\\n   JSScript (executable bytecode)\\n        ↓\\n   Interpreter::run() or JIT Compilation\\n```\\n\\nKey architectural patterns:\\n- **Template-based polymorphism** for character types (char16_t vs Utf8Unit) and parse modes (full vs. syntax)\\n- **Two-phase compilation**: First create intermediate stencil data, then instantiate to GC objects\\n- **Lazy compilation**: Functions can be compiled on-demand rather than eagerly\\n- **Scope tracking**: Binding information flows through parsing and bytecode emission phases\\n- **Error recovery**: Errors are reported with source locations and context information\\n\\nThis design allows SpiderMonkey to efficiently compile JavaScript across different character encodings, support both immediate and deferred compilation, and enable various optimizations at each stage.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
